## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: The task seeks the stress-strain-temperature relationship for a material, which is a core problem in constitutive modeling. Stress typically increases with strain via hardening laws and decreases with temperature via thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook simplified (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal term: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * ((T - c3) * c4)**c5) (power-law hardening with homologous temperature softening)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 / T)) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Swift with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power-law with exponential thermal softening)
- Linear hardening with exponential softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (simple combined model)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or early plastic behavior)
- Zener-Hollomon inspired: sigma = c0 * T * log(c1 * epsilon + 1) (logarithmic hardening scaled by temperature)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(c3 * (c4 / T))) (Sellars-Tegart / Garofalo type)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) to capture Voce-type saturation of stress at large strains
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiply strain-dependent terms by a decreasing function of T such as (c0 - c1*T) or exp(-c*T)
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) terms reflect dislocation motion governed by thermal activation energy
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in (c0 + f(epsilon)) represents initial yield stress before hardening
- Shifted power law for pre-strain → (epsilon + c0)**c1 accounts for materials with initial offset or pre-existing dislocation density
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as (T - c0)*c1 raised to a power, normalizing by reference/melting temperature
- Logarithmic hardening at large strains → log(1 + c*epsilon) captures diminishing hardening rate typical of stage III/IV hardening
- Multiplicative decomposition → Stress = f(epsilon) * g(T) assumes separable strain hardening and thermal softening contributions

**GT:** `-0.5450*(T - 352.16) + 1.5180*epsilon^0.6262*(T - 352.16)`

Simplifying GT:
`(T - 352.16) * (-0.5450 + 1.5180*epsilon^0.6262)`
`= T*(-0.5450 + 1.5180*epsilon^0.6262) + 352.16*(0.5450 - 1.5180*epsilon^0.6262)`
`= -0.5450*T + 1.5180*T*epsilon^0.6262 + 192.03 - 534.38*epsilon^0.6262`

So GT has the form: `T*a + T*b*epsilon^0.6262 + constant + d*epsilon^0.6262`

Key basis functions in GT (as functions of T and epsilon):
- T (linear in T, no epsilon)
- T*epsilon^0.6262 (product of T and fractional power of epsilon)
- constant term
- epsilon^0.6262

Note: c2 ≈ 0.6262, which is NOT 1/3 ≈ 0.3333, NOT 1, NOT any simple rational number.

This is critical: most candidates use `epsilon**(1/3)` as a basis function, but GT uses `epsilon**0.6262`. These are fundamentally different basis functions and cannot be made equivalent.
